<script>
      var googletag = googletag || {};
      googletag.cmd = googletag.cmd || [];
      googletag.cmd.push(function () {
          googletag.pubads().disableInitialLoad();
      });

      pbjs.que.push(function () {
          pbjs.addAdUnits(adUnits);
          pbjs.enableAnalytics([{
                provider: 'pubwise',
                options: {
                    site: 'd2a5ef67-8fed-4d00-9918-927ea7374a10',
                    endpoint:'https://api.pubwise.io/api/v4/event/add/'
                    }
                }]
          );
          pbjs.requestBids({
              bidsBackHandler: sendAdserverRequest
          });
      });

      function sendAdserverRequest() {
          if (pbjs.adserverRequestSent) return;
          pbjs.adserverRequestSent = true;
          googletag.cmd.push(function () {
              pbjs.que.push(function () {
                  pbjs.setTargetingForGPTAsync();
                  googletag.pubads().refresh();
              });
          });
      }

      setTimeout(function () {
          sendAdserverRequest();
      }, PREBID_TIMEOUT);

</script>

                        <div class="player-info-bio">

                    <tr><td><hr class="player-page-info-sep"/><div class="player-page-rotowire"><strong><a href="https://www.rotowire.com/users/ad_jump.asp?id=688&playerid=12588">RotoWire News</a>:</strong> Manager Dave Roberts is considering batting Puig third to begin the year while Justin Turner (wrist) heals on the disabled list, Doug Padilla of MLB.com reports.                     <td>8/17/2017</td><td class="td-badge"><div class="rg badge">RG</div></td><td><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/yasiel-puig-entices-yet-again/">Yasiel Puig Entices Yet Again</a><span class="m_author"> by <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/index.php?author=35849">Scott Spratt</a></span></td></tr></table></div></td></tr>

        </td>
        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
        
        
        
        
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Before there was Hanley Ramirez or Adrian Gonzalez or Brandon League, there was Yasiel Puig, whose seven-year, $42 million contract proved to be the first indication of the new Dodger financial might. Puig showed himself to be an impressive physical specimen and displayed very good raw talent & power in putting up a 1.076 OPS in 95 plate appearances in the low minors, but an elbow infection prevented him from collecting needed plate appearances in the Arizona Fall League. "Raw" is indeed the word there, since Puig has played so little organized ball over the last two seasons, and so it's likely that he spends the bulk of 2013 at Double-A. Despite the crowded Dodger outfield, Puig isn't being paid to be depth, so there will be room for him when he's ready; it's not out of the question that he makes his debut in the latter half of the season. (<a href="http://www.twitter.com/mike_petriello">Mike Petriello</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Muscular 21-year-old Puig signed a shocking contract that rocked the sport as the last Cuban bonus baby, then showed off prodigious power in limited minor league playing time.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>So... anything interesting happen with Yasiel Puig in 2013? No? Okay. After setting completely unreasonable expectations in spring training, Puig arrived in early June to actually meet -- perhaps exceed -- those expectations. He homered twice in his second game and four times in his first five; his batting average didn't drop below .350 until his 81st game in the bigs. Along the way, pitchers began to work out his weakness for bad breaking pitches, but even that was a mere speed bump, because he showed increased patience by topping a 10% walk rate in both August and September. If there is a flaw, his high whiff rate may portend a bigger strikeout rate and a lower batting average in 2014, but he should overcome that easily. A true five-tool player who can contribute in every fantasy category, his first full season in 2014 is highly anticipated... if he can manage to stop infuriating umpires, writers, opponents, and traffic cops along the way. <a href="http://www.twitter.com/mike_petriello">(Mike Petriello)</a><br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Yasiel Puig isn't the best player in baseball, but he's certainly the most exciting, in ways both good and bad. How he adjusts to his second season in the bigs will be a big test, though the potential here is so massive that fantasy players will rightfully draft him highly.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Was Yasiel Puig's second season a success or a disappointment? It depends on how you look at it. In nearly 200 additional plate appearances, he hit three fewer homers, stole the same amount of bases, and saw a drop-off in each of the three triple-slash stats. On the other hand, he walked more while striking out less, and are we really complaining about a 147 weighted runs created plus? Hampered by several nagging injuries down the stretch and weighed down by a very visible strikeout streak in the NLDS, there's a narrative that Puig had a lousy second half, but that was almost entirely due to a brutal August -- he did, after all, hit .284/.376/.432 in September. If we've learned anything about Puig, it's that he's unlikely to be the 40-homer guy his physique suggests he will be, but he's cemented his place as one of the ten best hitters in baseball, and he's only just entering his age-24 season. (<a href="http://www.twitter.com/mike_petriello">Mike Petriello</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Puig's second season wasn't as impressive in terms of raw counting stats, but his improvement in plate discipline puts him in position for a huge 2015, one that cements him as the superstar that fits the reputation he's collected.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>2015 was nothing short of a disaster for Yasiel Puig. He still posted above-average offense with a 111 weighted runs created-plus in the 79 games he played, but that was little solace to the fantasy owners who expected far more from the Cuban outfielder than the .255/.322/.436 slash line and 11 homers. Of the many distressing signs was a step backward in his plate discipline: his strikeout and walk rates regressed after he improved between his first two big league seasons, and he returned to chasing pitches out of the strike zone  particularly over the outer half  at an above-average rate. Reaching for pitches sent his soft/hard contact rates drifting in the wrong directions, his ground ball to fly ball ratio dropped, and his batting average on balls in play, notably one of his strengths through his first two seasons, regressed below .300. Then there were the off-the-field issues: a left hamstring strain vaporized his May, a right hamstring strain kept him off the field for all of September, he got into a bar fight in November, and word is <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/articles/2597460-is-there-anybody-left-in-los-angeles-whom-yasiel-puig-hasnt-alienated?utm_source=twitter.com&utm_medium=share&utm_campaign=web-des-art-bot-112">getting out</a> that he is a serious clubhouse problem. These are disturbing issues, though Puig is still just 25 and is likely going to be significantly discounted on draft day, and hes demonstrated that he can be a fantasy force when all is going right. Hes one of the most intriguing risk/reward investments for brave fantasy owners. (<a href="https://twitter.com/Karl_de_Vries">Karl de Vries</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Hamstring issues bit heavily into Yasiel Puigs playing time in 2015, though steps backward in his approach at the plate didnt help, either. Hes demonstrated his all-star talent at the major league level before, and after a disastrous 2015, likely has nowhere to go but up, but prudent fantasy owners in standard mixed leagues would do best to not count on him as better than a third outfielder.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Puig is one of the most naturally talented and athletically gifted players in all of baseball. Yet, his inability to stay healthy, prepare effectively and put it all together has been missing in the last two seasons. He was a league-average hitter and a decent defender. He wasn't the impactful fantasy option many have come to suspect. His offensive production has fallen in four consecutive seasons in part due to injury, but also out of stubbornness. Puig was demoted to Triple-A in August after the Dodgers acquired Josh Reddick from the A's. He was recalled in September and performed well: .281/.338/.561, 137 wRC+, .281 ISO. It came in just 65 plate appearances, but it was enough to land him on the Dodgers' postseason roster. As a 26-year-old, he should be entering the prime of his career. Instead, he's entering a season full of question marks. He'll need to improve on- and off-the-field (preparation-wise) if he hopes to be anything close to the player he was just two short years ago. (Dustin Nosler)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Puig has vastly under-performed over the last two seasons, with his 2016 season sticking out like a sore thumb. He had a career-low in walk rate, slugging, ISO, wRC+ and WAR. Heading into his prime, he should be able to turn things around, provided he stays healthy and does the things he needs to do to be successful.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
</table>

            <td align="left" style="width: 175px">
                <div id="SeasonStats1_tsStats" class="RadTabStrip RadTabStrip_FanGraphs RadTabStripTop_FanGraphs RadTabStripTop">
		<div class="rtsLevel rtsLevel1">
			<ul class="rtsUL"><li class="rtsLI rtsFirst rtsLast"><a class="rtsLink rtsSelected" href="statss.aspx?playerid=14225&amp;position=OF"><span class="rtsOut"><span class="rtsIn"><span class="rtsTxt">Batting</span></span></span></a></li></ul>

            <td align="right" style="width: 805px">
